ISPE Baseline Guide Vol. 3 (3rd Ed.) | p9 – p16

Learning Objectives / 學習目標

  1. 了解 ISPE Baseline Guide Volume 3 的定位與適用範圍，區分其與 PDA 技術報告（科學導向）在工程設計導向上的差異
  2. 掌握無菌產品製造設施設計的核心原則：Quality by Design (QbD)、風險導向方法、以及 CQA/CPP 如何驅動設施設計決策
  3. 理解 RABS (限制進出屏障系統)、Isolator (隔離器) 與傳統潔淨室技術在污染控制中的角色定位，以及人員作為最大污染源的關鍵概念
  4. 掌握第三版相較第二版的主要變更重點，包括環境分級的全球統一命名法、HVAC 設計更新、以及 LP/GAAS 概念的新增

Section Contents / 本章目錄

1.1 Background 1.2 Scope and Purpose 1.3 Key Features 1.4 Terminology 1.5 Changes Since Previous Edition 1.6 Legacy Facilities

1.1 Background 1.1 背景

1.1 Background

The design, construction, commissioning, and qualification of pharmaceutical facilities present significant challenges to manufacturers, engineering professionals, and equipment suppliers. These facilities are required to meet GMP regulations while remaining in compliance with other governing codes, laws, and regulations.

Lack of understanding of regulatory requirements may cause investment and operational costs to escalate. This Guide is intended to offer a consistent interpretation, while allowing a flexible and innovative approach to facility design, construction, commissioning, and qualification.

This Baseline Guide takes into account the FDA Pharmaceutical GMPs for the 21st Century – A Risk-Based Approach and the FDA September 2004 Guidance for Industry: Sterile Drug Products Produced by Aseptic Processing – Current Good Manufacturing Practice (which supersedes the 1987 Guideline on Sterile Drug Products Produced by Aseptic Processing). It also refers to Annex 1 of the European Union GMPs, which was last updated in November 2008. Another significant change since the original ISPE Sterile Guide was published, is that ISO 14644-1 has replaced US Federal Standard 209E Airborne Particulate Cleanliness Classes in Cleanrooms and Clean Zones. The reader also should be aware that there are other standards and guidance available in this subject area, such as ISO 13408-1.

This Guide is based on US and European Union (EU) requirements. This third edition has harmonized these requirements as much as possible, based on the experience of the authors. For further information regarding changes associated with the third edition, see Section 1.5.

教學解析

核心概念：ISPE Baseline Guide 的定位

ISPE Baseline Guide (基準指南) 是工程導向的技術文件，與 PDA Technical Report (科學導向) 的差異在於：

  • ISPE：聚焦設施設計 (Facility Design)、建造、調試與確認 (C&Q)
  • PDA：聚焦製程科學、微生物學、無菌保證

兩者互補，在實務中經常交叉引用。

重要時間軸提醒

本指南出版於 2018 年，引用的 EU GMP Annex 1 (GMP 附件一) 版本為 2008 年版。然而，EU GMP Annex 1 已於 2022 年完成重大修訂（2023 年 8 月正式生效），引入了 Contamination Control Strategy (CCS, 污染控制策略) 等全新要求。

閱讀本指南時，應同步參照 2022 版 Annex 1 的更新要求。

比喻：為什麼需要 Baseline Guide？

想像你要蓋一間無塵室工廠：法規告訴你「需要達到 ISO 5 等級」，但沒告訴你牆壁用什麼材質、空調怎麼設計、走道寬度多少。ISPE Baseline Guide 就像「建築師的參考手冊」，將法規要求轉化為可執行的工程設計方案。

關鍵法規參考文件

  • FDA Aseptic Guidance (2004) — 美國 FDA 無菌製程指引
  • EU GMP Annex 1 (GMP 附件一) — 歐盟無菌製造附件
  • ISO 14644 (潔淨室標準) — 取代美國舊制 Federal Standard 209E
  • ISO 13408 (無菌製程標準) — Aseptic Processing (無菌製程) 要求

1.2 Scope and Purpose of This Guide 1.2 本指南範圍與目的

1.2 Scope and Purpose of This Guide

This Guide may be used by industry for the design, construction, commissioning, and qualification of sterile product manufacturing facilities. It is neither a standard nor a GMP regulation. It is not intended to replace governing laws, codes, guidelines, standards, or regulations that apply to facilities of this type. The use of this document for new or existing facilities is at the discretion of the facility owner or operator.

The purpose of this Guide is to focus on facility engineering issues and how to provide cost effective facilities which make best use of available modern technologies to ensure that products of the highest quality are consistently manufactured. Where non-engineering issues are covered (e.g., microbiological topics, operational issues unrelated to the facility), the information is included to show engineers the importance of such topics and the impact they have on facility design. Therefore, these non-engineering topics are not covered comprehensively. Specific advice from Quality Assurance (QA) should be sought where additional information is required.

This Guide covers facilities for aseptic processing and terminal sterilization of Active Pharmaceutical Ingredients (APIs) and formulated products, generally for parenteral use. It is applicable to formulations that use APIs devised from either conventional chemistry or biopharmaceutical processing.

This Guide is focused on commercial scale medicinal sterile production. It does not cover medical devices. It does cover the facility aspects of sterile APIs but it does not cover the upstream process controls and equipment aspects of sterile APIs, details of which are covered in ISPE Baseline Guide: Active Pharmaceutical Ingredients (Second Edition).

Note: Many aspects of the guidance contained in this document (e.g., environmental and engineering matters) may be applicable to the manufacture of clinical supplies, Investigational Medicinal Products (IMP), sterile medical devices, and sterile drug/device combinations, as well as veterinary injectable products. Specific "specialty" sterile products (e.g., radiopharmaceuticals) are not covered in this Guide and may require additional controls, safeguards and regulations.

It is a principle of US and European GMP that when sterile APIs are manufactured, and the sterility is carried forward into the dosage form without change, then the dosage form GMP apply to both the sterile API manufacture and dosage form formulation.

This Baseline Guide takes into account the similar requirements of the GMPs of regulatory agencies from the US, EU, and those expressed in the Pharmaceutical Inspection Convention and Pharmaceutical Inspection Co-operation Scheme (PIC/S) and World Health Organization (WHO).

It is also recognized that some International Conference on Harmonisation (ICH) documents, which are applicable to products that may supply the US, EU, or Japan, should be considered for sterile product facilities. Since the original Sterile Manufacturing Facilities Baseline Guide was published, several papers and references have been produced, such as ICH Q8, ICH Q9, and ICH Q10.

This is the third edition of ISPE Baseline Guide: Sterile Product Manufacturing Facilities, which was originally issued in January 1999. It has been updated to reflect changes in regulations and industry practice, but it also takes into account that over the past few years several new ISPE Baseline Guides have been issued or re-issued.

教學解析

核心概念：本指南的法律地位

ISPE Baseline Guide 不是法規，也不是標準。它是業界公認的「最佳工程實務」參考文件。在法規稽核中，稽核員可能引用 ISPE Guide 來評估設施設計是否符合當前業界標準，但企業沒有法律義務完全遵守。

然而，若設計明顯偏離 Baseline Guide 的建議，企業需準備充分的科學與工程依據來支持其設計選擇。

適用範圍：兩大製造路線

本指南涵蓋兩種無菌產品製造設施 (Sterile Product Manufacturing Facility, 無菌產品製造設施)：

  • Aseptic Processing (無菌製程)：產品成分分別滅菌後，在無菌環境下組合充填。設施要求最高（需 ISO 5/Grade A 環境）。
  • Terminal Sterilization (終端滅菌)：產品充填封裝後，以最終包裝形式進行滅菌。設施要求相對較低，但仍需控制 bioburden。

比喻：無菌製程 vs 終端滅菌

無菌製程 (Aseptic Processing) 就像在手術室裡做手術 — 全程都要保持無菌狀態，任何一個環節的污染都可能導致失敗。終端滅菌 (Terminal Sterilization) 則像是把食物罐裝後再高溫殺菌 — 充填過程中容許較低的控制等級，因為最後會整體滅菌。

工程視角 vs 科學視角

本指南明確指出其焦點是設施工程議題。涉及微生物學或操作層面的內容僅為讓工程師了解其對設計的影響。若需深入的微生物或品質保證知識，應參考：

  • PDA TR13：環境監測 (Environmental Monitoring)
  • PDA TR22：製程模擬 (Process Simulation)
  • PDA TR90：污染控制策略 (CCS)

ICH Q-Trio 與設施設計

  • ICH Q8：Pharmaceutical Development — Quality by Design (QbD, 品質源於設計) 的基礎
  • ICH Q9：Quality Risk Management — 風險評估工具（FMEA、FTA 等）
  • ICH Q10：Pharmaceutical Quality Systems — 品質體系的持續改善框架

這三份文件構成了「以科學與風險為基礎」的品質管理架構，直接影響設施設計決策。

CDMO 實務應用

作為 CDMO（委託開發暨製造組織），本指南的適用範圍特別重要：

  • CDMO 的設施需同時滿足多個客戶的產品需求，設計時需考慮最大公約數
  • 客戶的產品可能涵蓋 Aseptic Processing 與 Terminal Sterilization，設施需具備彈性
  • 本指南明確指出適用於「conventional chemistry 或 biopharmaceutical processing」的 API — 涵蓋化學藥與生物製劑，與 CDMO 的多元產品組合一致

1.3 Key Features of This Guide 1.3 本指南主要特點

1.3 Key Features of This Guide

The following key principles are integral to this Guide:

  • The need to understand product and process requirements
  • Use of risk-based approaches
  • Concept of Good Engineering Practice (GEP)
  • Role of terminal sterilization and aseptic processing as mechanisms for producing sterile products
  • Protection of the product and the importance of understanding the most critical process steps
  • Management of flow and movement of personnel and materials
  • Importance of an integrated facility design approach
  • Understanding the principles of "open processing" and "closed processing", and how they affect the specification of the surrounding controlled environment
  • Role of barrier and isolator technology
  • Role of automation and robotics
  • Use of consistent HVAC terminology
  • Principles and understanding of "in operation" and "at rest" conditions for classified environments
  • Selection of appropriate materials and finishes
  • Importance of Environmental, Health and Safety (EH&S) issues as part of the design and operation
  • Reference to sterile APIs and link to ISPE Baseline Guide: Active Pharmaceutical Ingredients (Second Edition)

Product and process requirements normally drive the fundamental layout of a sterile product manufacturing facility. The Critical Quality Attributes (CQA) of the product should be understood. Significant sources of variability, which are Critical Process Parameters (CPP), can be determined from the CQA. For example, terminal sterilization is recommended wherever it can be applied; but where the product is affected significantly by this process step, product requirements may take precedence and other controlled methods of manufacturing may be used. This Guide seeks to make distinctions, where relevant, between aseptically processed products and those that are terminally sterilized.

The processing department (normally made up of the support areas and the processing core area) is the area where the product is formulated, filled into containers (usually vials, ampoules, pre-filled syringes, flexible bags, etc.), and the containers are sealed and secured. Protection of the product and container/closures from bio-contamination during these operations is considered critical.

Personnel are normally the greatest potential source of particulate and microbiological challenge to the process; therefore, any interface between personnel and the environment where sterile materials, products, components, and contact surfaces are exposed should be minimized. Consideration of all features should be taken into account, to produce an integrated facility design and to achieve a logical separation of clean and dirty operations. Available environmental control technologies should be used where possible, including:

  • Restricted Access Barrier Systems (RABS)
  • Isolators
  • Blow, Fill, and Seal (BFS) technology
  • Personnel gowning

The use of so-called conventional cleanroom technology may be acceptable for the processing of terminally sterilized products and APIs and products where there are technical issues which prevent the use of barrier technology for aseptic processing. Such choices have a fundamental effect on the design and operation of a facility, and should be considered at an early stage.

Documents that provide information on sterile products manufacturing facilities may use different terminology, particularly for environmental classifications (e.g., Class 100, ISO 5, or Grade A). This third edition of the Guide is intended to harmonize environmental classifications to help manufacturers to comply with regulations.

Facilities should be designed to ensure that the "in operation" condition during manufacture is met. Engineers and designers should also consider ensuring that the "at rest" condition is met. Although the principles behind the US and EU air classification terminologies are similar (particularly for the "in operation" condition), there is no commonly agreed global nomenclature to cover both the "at rest" and "in operation" conditions.

This Guide provides a tabular comparison of these various standards and guides and, in order to achieve clarity in the text, uses a single nomenclature to define the different process areas.

Fundamental requirements for facilities used for the manufacture of sterile products are the control principles offered by HVAC systems. In particular, engineers should understand that the environmental performance during "in operation" conditions is the time when the product and sterile package components are most likely to be exposed. The HVAC design and area classifications should ultimately relate to this condition.

Engineers and designers should understand the sources of particulate and bio-contamination, and the various ways that air quality can be maintained during manufacturing, such as:

  • Air filtration
  • Airflow uniformity control and direction
  • Differential cleanliness cascades
  • Room pressure differentials
  • Effective bio-contamination dilution

Engineers and designers should understand the importance of avoiding cross-contamination, which is a key factor that can influence HVAC design.

This Guide also is applicable to the selection of materials and finishes. A lifecycle approach should be taken when selecting materials to ensure a balance between the initial cost and expected life.

From a product point of view, it is important to understand the following concepts of Pharmaceutical Development (as embodied in ICH Q8, ICH Q9, and ICH Q10) and how they relate to product quality:

  • Quality by Design (QbD)
  • Quality Risk Management
  • Pharmaceutical Quality Systems

This Guide refers to these guidelines, as appropriate, to the design of facilities. It also supports taking a risk-based approach as this helps to assure the final facility meets the often demanding product requirements.

GEP should be applied to a facility to ensure that the most effective and efficient design solution is found, consistent with meeting manufacturing and quality needs.

教學解析

核心概念：CQA 與 CPP 驅動設施設計

本指南的核心設計哲學是：產品的品質屬性 (CQA) 決定製程參數 (CPP)，製程參數決定設施規格。這是 Quality by Design (QbD, 品質源於設計) 在設施工程上的體現。

  • Critical Quality Attributes (CQA, 關鍵品質屬性)：例如無菌性、微粒數、內毒素水平
  • Critical Process Parameters (CPP, 關鍵製程參數)：例如充填速度、環境溫濕度、壓差
  • 設施設計：HVAC 規格、潔淨室分級、屏障技術選擇

設施設計決策鏈

產品 CQA (無菌性、微粒)
    ↓ 定義
製程 CPP (充填環境、壓差、換氣次數)
    ↓ 驅動
設施規格 (潔淨室等級、HVAC、屏障技術)
    ↓ 影響
投資與營運成本

最重要的一句話

「Personnel are normally the greatest potential source of particulate and microbiological challenge to the process.」

人員是無菌製程中最大的污染來源 — 這個觀念是所有屏障技術（RABS、Isolator）發展的根本驅動力。整個設施設計的核心目標之一，就是將人員與產品之間的接觸介面最小化。

比喻：Open vs Closed Processing

Open Processing（開放式製程）：產品暴露在環境中，就像在開放式廚房裡做菜 — 環境品質直接影響食物品質。需要 ISO 5/Grade A 環境。

Closed Processing（封閉式製程）：產品在密封系統中流動，就像管路輸送 — 週圍環境的要求可以降低。

「In Operation」vs「At Rest」

  • In Operation（運行狀態）：設備運轉、人員在場、正常生產中。這是最嚴格的測試條件，也是法規真正關注的狀態。
  • At Rest（靜態）：設備已安裝完成但未運轉、無人員在場。主要用作系統性能基準 (benchmark)。

EU GMP Annex 1 對兩種狀態都有微粒限值要求；FDA 指引主要關注 in operation。第三版指南致力於統一全球命名法。

HVAC 設計的五大空氣品質控制手段

  1. Air Filtration（空氣過濾）：HEPA 濾網（H14, 99.995%）
  2. Airflow Uniformity（氣流均勻性）：單向流 (unidirectional airflow) 於關鍵區域
  3. Cleanliness Cascades（潔淨度層級）：從高潔淨區到低潔淨區的梯度設計
  4. Pressure Differentials（壓差）：正壓保護高潔淨區
  5. Bio-contamination Dilution（生物污染稀釋）：足夠的換氣次數

思考練習

  1. 如果你的產品可以承受終端滅菌（Terminal Sterilization），但客戶堅持使用無菌製程（Aseptic Processing），你會如何建議？這對設施設計有什麼影響？
  2. 在設計新的充填線時，選擇 RABS 還是 Isolator？列出三個關鍵考量因素。
  3. Good Engineering Practice (GEP) 與 GMP 的關係是什麼？為什麼本指南特別強調 GEP？

1.4 Terminology Used in This Guide 1.4 本指南使用的術語

1.4 Terminology Used in This Guide

The terminology for environmental classification levels, used throughout this Guide, is described in Chapter 2.

The conventions for referring to Good Manufacturing Practices differ in various regulatory communities. In the US, the acronym cGMP is used, while in Europe, Japan, and other areas the acronym is simplified to GMP. The "c" in cGMP stands for "current." For purposes of simplicity and harmonization, this Guide uses GMP. Where this term applies to US facilities or regulations, it is understood to mean cGMP.

教學解析

GMP vs cGMP — 有什麼差別？

cGMP（current Good Manufacturing Practice）是美國 FDA 使用的術語，「c」代表「current（現行）」，強調法規要求是動態演進的，企業必須跟上最新的技術水準。

GMP 是歐盟、日本、PIC/S 等地區使用的術語。

本指南統一使用 GMP，但當涉及美國法規時，應理解為 cGMP。實務上兩者意涵相同。

環境分級命名法的混亂

在無菌製造領域，同一個潔淨度等級有多種命名：

第三版指南採用「雙重標示法」（如 ISO 5/Grade A）來統一命名，詳見 Chapter 2。

1.5 Changes Since the Previous Edition of This Guide 1.5 與前版的變更

1.5 Changes Since the Previous Edition of This Guide

There are numerous changes within this Guide. An overview of the major changes for the third edition of this Guide is listed below:

  • A global facility design approach is now the basis for this Guide, with examples of RABS, full isolator, and BFS recommended layouts (see Chapter 4).
  • Area classifications have been normalized and harmonized to show the alignment of FDA and EU requirements. This mirrors the approach used in ISPE Baseline Guide: Biopharmaceutical Manufacturing Facilities (Second Edition):
    • ISPE classification grades have been deleted and replaced with harmonized dual designations (e.g., Grade 5 has been replaced with ISO 5/Grade A).
    • Area classification terms "Controlled Not Classified" (CNC) and "Unclassified" (UC) are no longer defined in the harmonized designations (Table 2.2). These terms are not part of the regulations, but are designations commonly used in the industry to differentiate respective areas (see Chapter 2).
  • Local Protection/Grade A Air Supply (LP/GAAS) for areas within lower classified areas has been added to Chapters 2 and 5.
  • Practical guidelines and practices for particulate monitoring have been added to this Guide.
Note: Users of this Guide should consider that in some circumstances, cost or single market focus could depart from the harmonized room classification design.

教學解析

第三版四大關鍵變更

  1. 全球化設計方法：不再分開討論美國與歐盟的設施設計，而是提供統一的全球化方案，包含 RABS、Isolator、BFS 三種技術的推薦佈局。
  2. 環境分級統一命名：廢除 ISPE 自訂分級（如 Grade 5），改用雙重標示法（ISO 5/Grade A）。同時取消 CNC 和 UC 的正式定義。
  3. LP/GAAS 概念新增：Local Protection/Grade A Air Supply — 在較低等級區域中提供局部 Grade A 空氣供應，適用於特定高風險操作點。
  4. 微粒監測指引：新增實務性的微粒監測操作指引。

比喻：雙重標示法為什麼重要？

想像你是一家跨國 CDMO，同時供貨給美國和歐洲客戶。美國客戶說「我要 ISO 5」，歐洲客戶說「我要 Grade A」— 其實他們要的是同一件事。雙重標示法（ISO 5/Grade A）消除了這種溝通混亂，讓全球化設施可以「一次設計、兩邊合規」。

LP/GAAS：局部保護的新概念

Local Protection/Grade A Air Supply (LP/GAAS) 是指在較低等級的環境（如 ISO 7/Grade B）中，針對特定操作點提供 Grade A 等級的局部空氣保護。

應用場景舉例：

  • 在 Grade B 環境中的滅菌後物料轉運口
  • 在 Grade C/D 環境中的取樣操作點
  • 需要局部高潔淨度但不需要整個房間升級的操作

CDMO 實務應用

對於同時供應美國市場與歐盟市場的 CDMO 而言，第三版的全球化設計方法尤其重要：

  • 採用雙重標示法可避免客戶稽核時的命名爭議
  • 全球化設施佈局設計一次性滿足 FDA 與 EMA 的要求
  • 若僅供應單一市場，可適度簡化設計以降低成本（如本節 Note 所述）

1.6 Considerations for Legacy Facilities 1.6 既有設施之考量

1.6 Considerations for Legacy Facilities

While the premise and focus of this Guide is directed at best practices for designing and constructing new facilities, the Guide can be useful in the renovation of older facilities to reduce the risk of non-sterility in order to comply with regulations.

Facility renovations and equipment upgrades/replacements can be a challenge to validated legacy systems. This Guide should serve as reference for updating facility and equipment to comply with these regulations.

For further insight into upgrading and replacing systems, see ISPE GAMP Good Practice Guide: The Validation of Legacy Systems.

教學解析

Legacy Facility（既有設施）的挑戰

本指南雖然以新建設施為主要對象，但明確指出也適用於既有設施的翻新改造。這在實務中非常重要，因為：

  • 大多數製藥設施都是在數十年前建造的，並非全新建設
  • 翻新既有設施需在「維持生產」和「符合新法規」之間取得平衡
  • 對已驗證的系統 (validated legacy systems) 進行變更需通過嚴謹的變更管制 (Change Control) 流程

比喻：老房子改造

翻新既有製藥設施就像改造一棟住人的老房子 — 你不能讓住戶搬出去再施工（因為要維持生產），你必須一邊住人一邊改建，而且每改一個地方都要確認不影響水電和結構安全（即驗證狀態）。

實務建議：漸進式升級策略

對於既有設施，建議採取風險導向的漸進式升級：

  1. 先進行 Gap Analysis（差距分析）：對照本指南與 2022 版 Annex 1，找出現有設施的差距
  2. 以風險評估排定優先順序：優先處理直接影響產品無菌性的項目
  3. 分階段實施：每次變更都經過驗證，不要一次大規模改造
  4. 參考 ISPE GAMP Good Practice Guide: The Validation of Legacy Systems

CDMO 實務應用

CDMO 的設施翻新面臨獨特挑戰：

  • 設施改造期間需維持對現有客戶的供貨承諾
  • 新增產線（如從 conventional cleanroom 升級至 RABS 或 Isolator）需重新驗證整個系統
  • 每次設施變更都需通知所有使用該設施的客戶（regulatory notification）
  • 建議建立「設施主計畫 (Facility Master Plan)」，將長期升級路線圖與客戶需求對齊
S

Section Summary / 本章總結

Chapter 1: Introduction — Key Takeaways

Key Takeaways

  • Positioning: ISPE Baseline Guide Vol. 3 is an engineering-focused reference for sterile product manufacturing facility design — not a regulation, but an industry-recognized best practice document.
  • Scope: Covers both aseptic processing and terminal sterilization facilities for APIs and formulated products (parenteral use), applicable to chemical and biopharmaceutical entities.
  • Design Philosophy: Product CQA drives CPP, which drives facility design specifications. Quality by Design (QbD) and risk-based approaches are foundational principles.
  • Personnel = #1 Contamination Source: This drives the adoption of barrier technologies (RABS, Isolators, BFS) to minimize human-product interface.
  • Harmonization: The 3rd edition unifies US and EU environmental classification nomenclature using dual designations (e.g., ISO 5/Grade A).
  • Key Regulatory References: FDA Aseptic Guidance (2004), EU GMP Annex 1, ISO 14644, ISO 13408, ICH Q8/Q9/Q10.
  • Legacy Facilities: The Guide is applicable to both new builds and renovations of existing facilities.

重點回顧

五個必記要點

  1. ISPE = 工程導向：與 PDA（科學導向）互補，專注於設施設計、建造、調試與確認
  2. CQA → CPP → 設施規格：品質源於設計 (QbD) 的設施工程應用
  3. 人員是最大污染源：所有屏障技術的發展都源於此核心認知
  4. 雙重標示法：ISO 5/Grade A 統一全球命名，消除跨區域溝通障礙
  5. 2022 Annex 1 更新：本指南（2018）出版後，EU GMP Annex 1 已於 2022 年完成重大修訂，閱讀時需同步參照最新版本

後續章節預告

  • Chapter 2：環境分級詳細定義（Cleanroom Classification, 潔淨室分級）
  • Chapter 4：RABS、Isolator、BFS 推薦佈局
  • Chapter 5：HVAC 系統設計
1a

Chapter 1a: 2a. Regulatory & Design (2.1–2.5)

法規與設計概念（上） | p17-p26

ISPE Baseline Guide Vol. 3 (3rd Ed.) | p17 – p26

Learning Objectives / 學習目標

  1. Understand the global regulatory landscape for sterile manufacturing (EU Annex 1, FDA, PIC/S, ICH) / 理解無菌製造的全球法規架構
  2. Differentiate terminal sterilization vs. aseptic processing and their facility impact / 區分終端滅菌與無菌製程對設施的影響
  3. Apply ICH Q9 risk assessment principles to facility design decisions / 應用 ICH Q9 風險評估原則於設施設計決策
  4. Explain the "Quality by Design" approach to sterile facilities / 解釋無菌設施的「品質源於設計」方法
  5. Compare contamination control approaches: conventional cleanrooms, RABS, and isolators / 比較污染控制方法：傳統潔淨室、RABS與隔離器
  6. Identify CQAs, CPPs, and critical process steps for sterile products / 辨識無菌產品的 CQA、CPP 與關鍵製程步驟

Section Contents / 章節目錄

2.1 Regulatory Guidance 2.2 Product Requirements 2.3 Risk Assessment 2.4 Risk Mitigation / QbD 2.5 Contamination Control

2.1 Regulatory Guidance / 法規指引

Original Text (ISPE Vol. 3)

2.1.1 Global Regulations and Guidance

Regulatory expectations for sterile drug products are defined throughout global regulations and guidance documents, including:

  • US FDA issued Guidance for Industry: Sterile Drug Products Produced by Aseptic Processing – Current Good Manufacturing Practice, which provides the FDA current thinking and is in addition to the Code of Federal Regulations (CFR).
  • EU Annex 1 Manufacture of Sterile Medicinal Products.
  • PIC/S, WHO and other regulatory bodies defined sterile product GMPs, which are mirrored after Annex 1.

In addition to regulations specific to sterile products, regions may also provide specific guidelines for "specialty" drug products, such as hormones, sensitizing compounds, biological preparations (including live viruses and spore formers), radiopharmaceuticals, and highly hazardous products.

The design concepts and philosophies presented in this Guide are intended to comply with the GMPs of most of the major global markets, including those regulated by the US FDA, EMA, WHO, and countries following PIC/S.

At the start of a project, all markets where the resulting manufactured products could be sold should be defined. The regulations for each region should be researched and understood, as there are both subtle and substantial differences between global market regulations.

Revisions to GMPs are made on a reoccurring basis. Regulated companies should investigate and understand all proposed changes and published standards by the governing bodies. Consideration should also be given to the evolving expectations of inspectors.

2.1.2 Current Guidance and Practices

Regulated companies should ensure that they are following the most recently published regulations and guidance documents. Regulatory guidance may follow and incorporate best practices that have already been adopted by industry.

Since the first edition of this ISPE Baseline Guide was issued in January 1999, there have been several new and revised regulatory guidance documents. Some examples of changes include:

  • Cleanroom design related to barrier technology and BFS / downgrading the background environment requirements
  • Gowning and movement in the aseptic processing area
  • Optimizing manual interventions with proper operator techniques and visualized airflow pattern analysis
  • Airflow velocity measurements (see Chapter 5)
  • Establishment and monitoring of differential pressures (DP) between areas of different classifications
  • Maintaining partially stoppered vials under ISO 5/Grade A conditions at all times until stopper is fully inserted and crimped
教學解說 / 實務觀點

法規架構總覽

核心概念：全球無菌製造法規三大支柱

無菌製造設施的設計必須同時滿足多個市場的法規要求，三大核心文件為：

  • 歐盟GMP附件一（EU GMP Annex 1）：全球最嚴格的無菌製造法規，2022年修訂版大幅強化污染控制策略（CCS）要求
  • FDA無菌製程指引（FDA Aseptic Guidance）：美國市場的核心要求，針對無菌製程提供具體操作指南
  • PIC/S：多數亞太國家（如台灣、新加坡、日本）採 PIC/S 體系，內容與歐盟 Annex 1 高度對齊

重點提示：法規區域差異

各國法規之間存在「微妙與重大」的差異。例如，美國 FDA 稽查員可能會期望看到歐盟 Annex 1 的要求在美國工廠中被採用。這種「交叉期望」趨勢在全球化稽查中越來越常見。

比喻：「最嚴標準」原則

想像不同國家的法規就像不同的考試：美國考數學、歐盟考物理、PIC/S考化學。作為全球供應商，你不能只準備一科——必須每科都達到最高標準。

法規演變與最佳實務

重點變化：從1999年至今的關鍵演進

ISPE指南列出的變化反映了行業趨勢：

  • 屏障技術普及：從傳統潔淨室轉向 RABS/隔離器
  • 人員管理強化：更嚴格的穿衣和移動管控
  • 氣流視覺化：強調煙霧測試與氣流模式分析
  • 半塞瓶管控：部分塞塞的瓶子必須始終保持在 ISO 5/Grade A 條件下

CDMO 實務應用

作為 CDMO，我們服務多個客戶，產品可能銷售到不同市場。因此：

  • 設施設計應採用「最嚴標準」原則，同時滿足 FDA + EU Annex 1 + PIC/S
  • 建立法規情報追蹤機制，定期監控各市場法規變化
  • 客戶引進時，首先確認目標市場，據此決定設施需求

2.2 Product Requirements / 產品需求

Original Text (ISPE Vol. 3)

2.2.1 Product Profile/Characteristics

Sterile products require rigorous control of potential contamination which may take the form of particulates, microorganisms, and endotoxins. There are two primary methods for producing sterile products:

  • Terminal sterilization
  • Aseptic processing

Generally, regulatory agencies have stated that, where possible (i.e., product is not affected or compromised by the terminal sterilization process), parenteral products should be terminally sterilized. Products should be developed from the outset to be terminally sterilized. Where this is not feasible without damaging the product, alternative processes, such as aseptic processing, can be employed.

The choice between the two processing routes has significant influence on:

  • Facility layout including process/production flow
  • Level of environmental classification
  • HVAC design
  • Subsequent Environmental Monitoring (EM)

In addition to the aseptic processing methodology, the equipment technology selected for contamination control (isolator, RABS, or BFS) or the use of conventional cleanroom technology also has a significant impact on planning, facility layout, equipment arrangements, area classifications, and HVAC system design.

Several key aspects of the products themselves need to be considered at an early stage, including whether the product:

  • Is a liquid, a suspension, an emulsion, a powder, semi-solid, or freeze-dried
  • Supports microbiological growth
  • Is potent, toxic, and/or radioactive
  • Is adversely impacted by exposure to light, oxygen, temperature, humidity/moisture
  • Is volatile
  • Is biologically active (e.g., live vaccines)

Additional product and process aspects influencing facility design include:

  • Presentation (vial, ampoule, syringes, bags, etc.)
  • Scale or capacity required
  • Cross-contamination potential in multi-product/multi-purpose facilities
  • Use of ready-to-use and single-use components and technology

2.2.2 Process Definition

The product(s) final form can influence processing conditions, equipment selection, and facility design. The facility layout is affected by:

  • Size of the product presentation
  • Capacity and throughput required
  • Number and variety of presentations to be processed
  • Potential flexibility to add or adjust presentations and products in the future

2.2.2.1 Product Critical Quality Attributes (CQAs)

CQAs are those physical, chemical, biological, or microbiological properties or characteristics that should be within an appropriate limit, range, or distribution to ensure the desired product quality. These can include:

  • Purity, Composition, Identity
  • Biological activity, Potency
  • Sterility and endotoxin limits
  • Particulates

2.2.2.2 Critical Process Parameters (CPPs)

CPPs include input settings/controls or output readings from process equipment or monitoring devices. These can include:

  • Temperature and the associated rate of change
  • Time, Flow rate and velocities
  • Pressure, pH, Conductivity

2.2.2.3 Critical Process Steps

Critical process steps should be defined for all product types. For aseptically manufactured products, the most critical steps are those during product transfers and when sterilized product and container/closure are exposed to the atmosphere or a surface. Examples include:

  • Sampling, weighing, and dispensing of materials
  • Preparation, sterilization, and depyrogenation of containers and closures
  • Aseptic connections and transfers (under ISO 5/Grade A)
  • Formulation and sterile filtration
  • Filling and primary sealing
  • Transfers to lyophilizers, loading/unloading, and final capping
  • Storage and transfer of sterilized equipment and components
  • Cleaning and sterilization of product contact equipment
教學解說 / 實務觀點

終端滅菌 vs. 無菌製程

比喻：餐廳食品安全

終端滅菌就像在廚房完成所有備料後，把整道菜放進烘箱高溫殺菌。即使備料過程不夠完美，最後的高溫處理可以補救。

無菌製程則像做壽司——每一個步驟都必須在極度清潔的環境下完成，沒有最後的「高溫補救」機會。

產品特性對設施的影響

重點：六大產品特性決定設施需求

設計階段必須提前考慮的產品特性：

  • 劑型：液體、懸浮液、粉末、凍乾等，直接影響設備選擇與空間配置
  • 微生物生長支持性：影響持有時間與環境控制要求
  • 毒性/放射性：需要專用設施或額外防護措施
  • 環境敏感度：光、氧、溫度、濕度敏感則需特殊設計
  • 揮發性：需要密閉系統與排氣控制
  • 生物活性：活病毒疫苗需專用設施

CQA、CPP 與關鍵製程步驟

核心概念：CQA 與 CPP 的關係

CQA（關鍵品質屬性）是產品必須滿足的品質標準（如無菌、微粒數、內毒素）。

CPP（關鍵製程參數）是影響 CQA 的製程條件（如溫度、時間、壓力）。

設施設計的目的就是確保能夠可靠地控制 CPP，進而達到 CQA 的要求。

ICH Q8/Q10 邏輯鏈

產品品質 = f(CQA)
CQA = f(CPP)
CPP = f(設施設計 + 製程控制)

∴ 設施設計 → CPP 控制 → CQA 達標 → 產品品質

重點：無菌製程八大關鍵步驟

以下每個步驟都可能引入污染，必須在設計階段就納入風險評估：

  1. 稱量與配料
  2. 容器/蓋子滅菌與除熱原
  3. 無菌連接與轉移
  4. 配方與無菌過濾
  5. 填裝與初級密封
  6. 凍乾機轉移與最終加蓋
  7. 滅菌設備儲存與轉移
  8. 清潔與滅菌

CDMO 實務應用

對於 CDMO 的多產品設施，產品需求分析特別重要：

  • 需要考慮「最惡情境產品」來設計設施（例如：最毒的、最敏感的、最難清潔的）
  • 凍乾產品需預留凍乾機空間，影響整體廠房布局
  • 單一使用技術（Single-Use）可大幅減少換線清潔驗證負擔
  • 未來彈性：預留增加新劑型或包裝的空間

2.3 Risk Assessment / 風險評估

Original Text (ISPE Vol. 3)

2.3 Risk Assessment

The US FDA GMP for the 21st Century initiative and global GMPs, such as ICH Q9, along with science and risk-based approaches, are fundamental to ensuring that products of the highest possible quality are manufactured. Sterile product manufacturing is recognized as requiring special steps to mitigate risk to product (particularly by bio-contamination); therefore, adequate controls should be established to minimize particulate and microbial ingress.

Risk assessments, using tools such as Failure Mode, Effects, and Criticality Analysis (FMECA), Hazard Analysis and Critical Control Points (HACCP), or other methods, are encouraged to ensure that product manufacturing risks are systematically understood, assessed, and controlled.

Reference should be made to Annex II within ICH Q9, which gives specific examples of quality risk management. ICH Q9 Annex II.4 covers risk management for Facilities, Equipment, and Utilities under the following headings:

  • Design of facility/equipment
  • Hygiene aspects in facilities
  • Qualification of facility/equipment/utilities
  • Cleaning of equipment and environmental control
  • Calibration/preventative maintenance
  • Computer systems and computer-controlled equipment

Risk assessments should be led by subject matter experts or a diversified team who understand the process and product critical aspects. In aseptic processing, risk assessments are performed for individual processes or production lines to identify hazards to product quality.

Risk is defined as the combination of the probability of occurrence of harm and the severity of that harm. Risk, when expressed in terms of Risk Priority Numbers (RPN), is a function of Severity, Probability of Occurrence, and Detectability. From this determination, mitigation and control options are developed to minimize risk to the product. Such options could involve engineering solutions, procedural solutions, or a combination of both.

教學解說 / 實務觀點

風險評估在設施設計中的角色

核心概念：ICH Q9 風險管理架構

ICH Q9 提供了系統性的風險管理方法，應用於製藥設施設計時包含六大領域：

  • 設施/設備設計：如潔淨室分區、氣流方向
  • 衛生面向：如表面材質、清潔可及性
  • 確認活動：IQ/OQ/PQ 的測試範圍
  • 清潔與環境控制：清潔驗證與環境監控
  • 校準/預防維護：關鍵儀器的校準頻率
  • 電腦化系統：SCADA、BMS 等控制系統

RPN 風險優先數 計算公式

RPN = 嚴重度 (S) x 發生機率 (O) x 可偵測性 (D)

其中：
  S (Severity)     = 1–10（危害嚴重程度）
  O (Occurrence)   = 1–10（發生機率）
  D (Detectability)= 1–10（不可偵測程度，10最難發現）

RPN 越高，需要優先處理。
超過門檻值的 RPN 必須制定緩解措施。

比喻：風險評估就像買保險

想像你在評估一棟房子的風險：

  • 嚴重度：如果房子着火，損失多大？
  • 發生機率：這個地區多常發生火災？
  • 可偵測性：有沒有煙霧警報器能及早發現？

製藥設施的風險評估邀輯完全相同——評估每個風險點，然後決定需要多少「保險」（工程或程序控制）。

重點：工程解決方案優先於程序解決方案

ISPE 強調：應優先考慮「工程解決方案」（Engineered Solutions）而非依賴「程序解決方案」（Procedural Solutions）。

例如：

  • 工程解決：安裝隔離器阻隔人員與產品接觸
  • 程序解決：SOP 要求人員穿戴無菌手套

工程解決更可靠，因為不依賴人員執行的一致性。

練習思考

在一條新的無菌填裝線設計中，如果你發現「人員在填裝區的介入頻率」的 RPN 超過門檻值，你會建議哪種緩解措施？

  • A. 加強人員無菌技術培訓（程序解決）
  • B. 導入 RABS 或隔離器減少介入（工程解決）
  • C. 增加環境監控頻率（可偵測性改善）

最佳策略通常是 B 優先，輔以 A 和 C。

2.4 Risk Mitigation / "Quality by Design" / 風險緩解與「品質源於設計」

Original Text (ISPE Vol. 3)

2.4 Risk Mitigation / "Quality by Design"

Pharmaceutical production facilities should be designed to promote and encourage good manufacturing processes. For such a design to occur, the risks associated with producing a quality product should be identified so they can be mitigated either by engineered solutions or by procedural solutions.

Engineered solutions should be considered before relying on procedures, wherever possible.

A "Quality by Design" process focuses on the operational or "future state" of the facility, and seeks to identify and mitigate risks that may occur during production. Solutions are defined and incorporated into the design and verified in the installed asset to ensure the facility produces quality products based on understanding the production requirements.

教學解說 / 實務觀點

QbD 在設施設計中的應用

核心概念：Quality by Design（品質源於設計）

QbD 的核心理念是：品質不是檢驗出來的，而是設計進去的。應用於設施設計時：

  • 理解生產需求：先明確要生產什麼、怎麼生產
  • 辨識風險：哪些生產步驟可能影響品質
  • 納入設計：將緩解措施融入設施設計
  • 驗證確認：通過確認活動驗證設計意圖已實現

比喻：蓋房子 vs. 消防安全

想像你在蓋一棟大樓：

  • 傳統做法：先蓋好，然後檢查是否符合消防法規，不符合就改
  • QbD 做法：從設計階段就把消防通道、灑水系統、防火材料融入建築設計

QbD 在製藥設施中就是後者——從一開始就把品質控制設計進設施中。

CDMO 實務應用

CDMO 設施的 QbD 特別挑戰：

  • 必須同時滿足多個客戶的品質需求，設計應基於最嚴格的需求
  • 彈性設計很重要：今天生產蛋白質藥物，明天可能是細胞治療
  • 設施生命週期內的法規變化需納入考量（如 Annex 1 修訂）
  • 設計階段的投資可以避免生產階段的巨額失敗成本

2.5 Contamination Control Approaches / 污染控制方法

Original Text (ISPE Vol. 3)

2.5 Contamination Control Approaches

The prevention of product contamination is the single largest objective in sterile product facilities. Eliminating product contamination is paramount, as every contaminated container has the potential to severely harm a patient.

Contamination is defined as the undesired introduction of impurities of a chemical or microbiological nature, or of foreign matter, into a raw material, intermediate, API, or product during production, sampling, packaging or repackaging, storage or transport.

Contamination can occur in two ways:

  • Environmental contamination results from the ingress of contaminants (microbiological, particulate, or foreign matter) from the surrounding production areas or even from outside environments.
  • Cross-contamination is contamination of a starting material, intermediate product, or finished product with another starting material or product during production. Cross-contamination results when APIs from one product find their way into another product.

2.5.1 Sources of Contamination

Particulate/foreign matter and bio-contamination usually occur in one of two ways:

  • Through mechanical transfer (e.g., via personnel, materials, or equipment)
  • Via airborne contaminants

Sources of cross-contamination include four primary routes: Mix-Up, Retention, Mechanical Transfer, and Airborne Transfer.

2.5.2 Contamination Control

Once sources of contamination have been identified, controls or procedures can be established. Most contamination can be controlled through measures such as:

  • Nested zones of protection including barrier technology around the most critical areas
  • Selecting closed processes and associated control systems
  • Removing sources of contamination
  • Use of pre-sterilized closed container systems and single-use aseptic connectors
  • Proper control of personnel, material, equipment and waste flow
  • Design and implementation of effective cleaning, disinfection, and sterilization procedures
  • Personnel gowning and hygiene
  • Employee training and control of the process environment

"Nested manufacturing zones" is the concept where critical aseptic zones are at the heart of the facility and are surrounded by lesser zones according to criticality and cleanliness. As materials and personnel pass from less critical to higher criticality areas, an improvement step occurs.

2.5.3 Approaches to Environmental Contamination Control

This Guide recognizes three approaches in increasing levels of separation effectiveness:

  1. Conventional cleanroom technology (batch operations and substantially open processing lines most vulnerable to contamination)
  2. RABS (Restricted Access Barrier Systems)
  3. Isolator technology

This edition recommends the use of barrier technology (isolators and RABS) for aseptic processing in new or renovated facilities. Barrier technology provides engineered separation and control rather than relying on the aseptic technique of an individual.

Effective environmental control requires:

  • Control of air filtration
  • Determination of airflow patterns
  • Control of temperature and humidity
  • Control of internally generated contamination by dilution or displacement
  • Segregation of zones by physical separation, pressurization, and/or airflow direction control

2.5.4 Cross-Contamination

Avoidance of cross-contamination to prevent carryover of one product into another must be considered. Under GMP, manufacturers may set cross-contamination limits on a substance-by-substance basis. In some forms, several products may pose a significant risk if they contaminate other products — for these products, separate production facilities, air handling equipment, and process equipment may be necessary.

教學解說 / 實務觀點

污染控制：無菌設施的核心任務

核心概念：兩種污染類型

  • 環境污染（Environmental Contamination）：來自周圍環境的微粒、微生物或異物入侵
  • 交叉污染（Cross-Contamination）：一個產品的成分混入另一個產品

每一個受污染的容器都可能嚴重傷害患者——這是無菌製造的最基本信念。

巢狀製造區概念

核心概念：Nested Manufacturing Zones（巢狀製造區）

無菌設施的空間配置遵循「由外到內、逐層淨化」的原則：

外部環境 / Unclassified
▼
Grade D / ISO 8（支援區）
▼
Grade C / ISO 7（準備區）
▼
Grade B / ISO 5（背景區）
▼
Grade A / ISO 5（填裝區 — 核心）

每一層轉換都需要「改善步驟」：物料清潔、人員更衣、氣壓階梯等。

三大污染控制技術

比喻：手術室的無菌層級

想像三種手術室設置：

  • 傳統潔淨室：醫生在潔淨房間裡直接操作，全靠手套和無菌技術
  • RABS：醫生透過一層透明屏障操作，可透過手套孔介入
  • 隔離器：醫生透過完全密封的手套箱操作，與產品完全隔離

隔離等級越高，對人員無菌技術的依賴越低。

重點：有效環境控制的五大要素

  1. 空氣過濾控制：HEPA 過濾器，確保空氣潔淨度
  2. 氣流模式確定：單向氣流（UAF）在關鍵區域提供保護
  3. 溫濕度控制：影響微生物生長和產品穩定性
  4. 內部污染稀釋/排除：通過換氣次數控制
  5. 區域隔離：物理分隔、壓差控制、氣流方向控制

CDMO 實務應用：多產品設施的污染控制

對於 CDMO 的多產品設施，污染控制是最大挑戰：

  • 環境污染：推薦採用隔離器或 RABS，降低對人員無菌技術的依賴
  • 交叉污染：應建立基於風險的清潔驗證策略，特別是高毒性/高效產品
  • 專用設施：對於細胞治療、活病毒疫苗等高風險產品，可能需要專用生產區域
  • 單一使用技術：大幅減少交叉污染風險，特別適合多產品切換

練習思考

你的 CDMO 設施需要同時生產一個高效致敏藥物和一個普通注射劑。你會如何設計設施布局？

  • 考慮：空氣處理系統是否需要獨立？
  • 考慮：人員、物料流向如何設計？
  • 考慮：清潔驗證策略如何制定？
  • 考慮：是否需要專用生產線？

Table 2.1: Sources of Contamination and Mitigation / 表 2.1：污染來源與緩解措施

Original Table (ISPE Vol. 3)
教學解說

三大污染類型對應策略

  • 非活性微粒：主要來自人員、設備磨損、空氣系統。核心對策是 HEPA 過濾+屏障技術+自動化
  • 活性微生物：最大來源是人員。隔離器和 RABS 是最有效的工程控制
  • 內毒素：與水和濕度密切相關。除熱原需要高溫（>250°C）或化學處理

重點：人員是最大污染源

在無菌環境中，人員是微粒和微生物的最大來源。這就是為什麼：

  • 隔離器和 RABS 被強烈推薦（減少人員接觸）
  • 自動化和機器人技術正在快速發展
  • 穿衣培訓和無菌技術培訓至關重要

Section Summary / 章節總結

Key Takeaways
  1. Regulatory Landscape: Facility design must satisfy multiple global GMP standards simultaneously (FDA, EU Annex 1, PIC/S). Cross-referencing expectations between markets is increasingly common during inspections.
  2. Terminal vs. Aseptic: Terminal sterilization is preferred when product stability permits. The choice fundamentally shapes facility classification, HVAC, layout, and environmental monitoring requirements.
  3. CQA-CPP-Facility Chain: Product CQAs drive CPPs, which in turn drive facility and equipment design requirements. This chain must be documented from design phase onward (ICH Q8/Q10).
  4. Risk-Based Design (ICH Q9): Use structured risk assessment tools (FMECA, HACCP) to identify and prioritize risks. Engineered solutions should always be preferred over procedural controls.
  5. Quality by Design: Build quality into the facility from the design phase rather than testing it in afterward. Focus on the operational "future state" of the facility.
  6. Contamination Control Hierarchy: Isolators > RABS > conventional cleanrooms. New facilities should adopt barrier technology. The "nested zones" concept with improvement steps at each transition is fundamental.
  7. Cross-Contamination: Multi-product facilities must address four contamination routes (mix-up, retention, mechanical, airborne) through both engineering and procedural controls.
重點回顧
  1. 法規架構：設施設計必須同時滿足多個市場的 GMP 要求。稽查員越來越頻繁地採用「交叉期望」標準。
  2. 終端滅菌 vs. 無菌製程：終端滅菌是法規首選。選擇哪種路徑決定了設施的根本設計方向。
  3. CQA-CPP-設施鏈：產品品質屬性驅動製程參數，製程參數驅動設施設計。必須從設計階段開始文件化。
  4. 風險導向設計：使用 FMECA、HACCP 等工具系統性評估風險。工程解決方案始終優先於程序解決方案。
  5. 品質源於設計：從設計階段就將品質控制融入設施，而非事後檢測。
  6. 污染控制階層：隔離器 > RABS > 傳統潔淨室。新建設施應採用屏障技術。「巢狀區域」概念是基本原則。
  7. 交叉污染：多產品設施必須針對四大路徑（混淆、殘留、機械轉移、氣傳）建立控制措施。
1b

Chapter 1b: 2b. Classification & Integration (2.6–2.10)

分類定義與整合設計（下） | p27-p36

ISPE Baseline Guide Vol. 3 (3rd Ed.) | p27 – p36

Learning Objectives / 學習目標

  1. Understand the harmonized area classification system (Grade A/B/C/D, ISO 5/7/8, Class 100/10K/100K) and the critical distinction between "at rest" and "in operation" conditions.
  2. Explain the role of hazard analysis and operator protection strategies, including containment for potent compounds.
  3. Differentiate between open and closed processing and their impact on required environmental classifications.
  4. Describe integrated facility design principles: zoning, material/personnel flow, and segregation.
  5. Identify additional considerations for multi-product facilities, campaign manufacturing, and lifecycle cost.

Section Navigation / 章節導覽

2.6 Area Classification Definitions 2.6.3 Classification for Process Stages 2.7 Hazard & Operator Protection 2.8 Open/Closed Processing 2.9 Integrated Facility Design 2.10 Other Considerations Section Summary
2.6

Area Classification Definitions

Harmonized designations, particle limits, microbial limits — p27–p30

Harmonized Classification System

The area classification nomenclature in this Guide uses established terminology required by many regulatory agencies worldwide. It allows the user to present their facility design using the terminology and requirements with which regulators are familiar.

There are key criteria that define the classification of a process area:

  • Whether the specification relates to the "in operation", "at rest", or both conditions
  • Microbiological limits
  • Total air particulate limits

The airborne particle size limits should be clearly defined when classifying an area by airborne particles. The assessment technique and microbial limits should be clearly defined when classifying the microbiological cleanliness of an area.

When reference is made to Cleanliness Grades A through D, note that these integrate "at rest" and "in operation" conditions with two particle sizes (0.5 µm and 5.0 µm) and microbial levels.

Although there are many similarities, regulatory requirements are not 100% consistent globally. Regulated companies should define requirements that account for the criteria specified for all markets where their products will be sold.

Table 2.2 shows harmonized designations and their correlation with the Class/Grade, particle size and count, and microbial limits of US FDA, EU Annex 1, and PIC/S guidelines. These three guidelines were chosen because many guidance documents written by agencies around the world are either based on the US FDA or EU Annex 1 or have adopted PIC/S as a global standard.

調和分級系統

核心概念：三大分級體系對照

全球無菌製造有三大分級體系，實務上必須熟悉並交叉對照：

  • EU/PIC/S：Grade A / B / C / D（A/B/C/D級潔淨區）
  • ISO 14644-1：ISO 5 / 7 / 8（ISO 5/7/8級）
  • 舊版 US FDA：Class 100 / 10,000 / 100,000

重點提示：靜態 vs 動態的關鍵區別

靜態（At Rest）：設備安裝完成、HVAC運作中，但無人員在場、無生產活動。

動態（In Operation）：正常生產運作中，人員在場、設備運轉。

EU Annex 1 定義兩種條件下的粒子限值；US FDA 則以動態條件為主。這是歐美法規的核心差異。

比喻說明：餐廳衛生檢查

想像衛生局檢查餐廳：「靜態」就像開店前檢查廚房是否乾淨；「動態」則是營業高峰期檢查，看廚師操作中能否維持衛生標準。無菌製造的「動態」標準永遠比「靜態」更難達成，因為人員是最大的污染源。

Table 2.2: Harmonized Designations (Simplified) / 調和分級對照表（簡化版）

Key Notes on Harmonization

  • The US FDA does not have an area classification equivalent to Grade D. Grade D is ISO 8 "at rest" only, and US FDA classifications are based on "in operation" conditions.
  • The "Controlled Not Classified" (CNC) designation is increasingly popular. It originated in biologics facilities for spaces that are access controlled and cleaner than general HVAC areas, but for which no formal classification claim is made.
  • A change of grade is typically associated with a change in the status of personnel or materials—usually achieved through clothing changes, cleaning/decontamination processes, or physical separation (RABS, isolators, UAF hoods).
  • For Grade A, there is no ISO 14644-1 classification for particles ≥5.0 µm at or below ISO 5. The EU Annex 1 limit of 20 particles/m³ has no ISO equivalent.

調和重點補充

實務陷阱：Grade D 的歐美差異

US FDA 沒有 Grade D 對應等級。當設計面向全球市場的設施時，Grade D 製造區可能需要以 ISO 8「動態」呈報給FDA。這對設施設計有直接影響：原本在歐洲可以用 Grade D 的工序，面向美國市場時可能需要升級到 ISO 8/Grade C。

CNC：控制但不分級區域

CNC（Controlled Not Classified）是近年越來越流行的概念，尤其在生物製品設施。這些區域有門禁管控、比一般HVAC更乾淨，但不做正式的潔淨等級聲明。可以用於檢驗、終端滅菌等支援區域。

2.6.3

Area Classification for Typical Process Stages

Environmental classifications per process step — p30–p33

Bioburden Control Strategy

The control of bioburden in aseptic processing and terminal sterilization should minimize the bioburden challenge to the sterilization process and ensure appropriate control of endotoxins that will not be inactivated or removed by the sterilization process.

Pre-sterilization bioburdens are controlled by deployment of an appropriately controlled immediate and surrounding process environment. For example, the air classification at the filling stage of terminally sterilized products may be controlled to a lesser standard than required for aseptic processing.

Different process steps normally require different environmental classifications. It is normal practice to cascade air quality from higher quality levels to lower quality levels (e.g., from ISO 5/Grade A critical areas to ISO 7/Grade B or ISO 8/Grade C areas).

Facilities designed for potent or biological products (viral or spore forming) may be required to place production areas within environments that are negative to the surrounding areas. A risk assessment should determine the risk of environmental exposure versus the risk of contaminating the product.

生物負荷控制策略

空氣質量級聯原則

無菌製造設施的空氣質量應從高到低級聯：

  • 核心區（ISO 5/Grade A）→ 背景環境（ISO 7/Grade B）→ 支援區（ISO 8/Grade C）→ 一般控制區（Grade D/CNC）

每一層級聯都通過壓差、氣流方向和物理屏障來維持。

特殊情況：高活性/生物製品的壓差反轉

一般無菌製造是正壓（內高外低）保護產品，但高活性藥物或病毒製品可能需要負壓（內低外高）以保護人員和外部環境。這需要風險評估來平衡產品保護與操作人員安全。

Table 2.3: Baseline Environmental Classification for Key Process Steps (Simplified) / 典型工序環境分級（簡化版）

Key Table Notes

  • LP/GAAS: Localized Protection / Grade A Air Supply — filtered air supply or physical containment/enclosure used to reduce risk of bio-contamination. The method depends on exposure and risk to the product or operator.
  • Isolator advantage: Where an isolator provides ISO 5/Grade A, the background environment can be reduced from ISO 7/Grade B to ISO 8/Grade C.
  • Terminal sterilization filling: EU Annex 1 permits filling at Grade C for terminally sterilized products if the product is not "at risk" (e.g., does not support microbial growth). If it does, higher standards apply.
  • Capping/crimping: Generates large quantities of particles; equipment should be separated from open container areas or include air extraction for particulate control.

表格重點解讀

比喻：開放式 vs 封閉式製程的保護等級

想像在戶外煉菜（開放製程）與在密封壓力鍋內煉菜（封閉製程）的差別。戶外需要更嚴格的防污染措施（遮蔽、潔淨環境），而壓力鍋本身就是屏障。同理，隔離器內的 ISO 5 環境允許背景降到 ISO 8/Grade C。

LP/GAAS 實務應用

LP/GAAS（局部保護/A級送風）是一種彈性的保護措施，不是完整的 ISO 5 環境，但提供過濾氣流來保護產品暴露點。常見於等級較低的區域（如 Grade C/D）中的關鍵操作點。

2.7

Hazard and Operator Protection

Containment, potent compounds, risk vs hazard — p33

Operator Protection Requirements

In addition to the design requirements for product protection, it is critical that engineers consider protection of the operator and the room environment, particularly if the product is potentially harmful if inhaled.

The key requirement for operator protection is to understand the difference between hazard and risk. The potential risk to the operator should be understood and appropriate mitigation to manage the level of risk should be defined.

A risk analysis should be performed to assess the potential for harm and an operator protection plan should be defined. Engineered approaches are preferred, because they typically remove the operator from the harmful situation. Examples include:

  • Utilizing containment isolators for potent compounds
  • Automating the movement of open containers, such as in lyophilization loading

The use of Personal Protective Equipment (PPE) should be employed only in breach situations, or as a secondary means of protection.

操作人員防護要求

危害（Hazard）vs 風險（Risk）

危害：物質本身的固有危險性（如高活性藥物的毒性）。

風險：危害造成傷害的可能性，考慮暴露途徑和防護措施。

工程控制（如隔離器、自動化）優於 PPE，因為工程控制從根源消除暴露，而 PPE 只是最後一道防線。

比喻：防護階層

就像處理危險化學品：最好的做法是封閉系統（工程控制），其次是通風櫥（管理控制），PPE 是最後手段。無菌製造中，封閉式隔離器同時保護產品和操作人員。

思考練習

您的設施要生產一種高活性藥物（OEL < 1 µg/m³）的無菌注射劑。如何同時滿足產品保護（正壓）和操作人員保護（負壓）的衝突需求？

  • 提示：考慮隔離器 + 氣鎖設計
2.8

Open/Closed Processing

Open vs closed process categories, environmental requirements — p33–p35

2.8.1 Open Processing / 開放製程

Definition and Examples

Open processing is a process condition when the product, materials, or container/closure surfaces are exposed to the immediate process environment at a stage/time when such exposure could influence the quality or purity of the product.

Examples of open processes include:

  • Open cleaned equipment post-sterilization
  • Loading and unloading an item or process equipment
  • Aseptic assembly of process equipment
  • Filling open product containers such as ampoules, vials, or syringes
  • Transporting a partially secure vial (uncapped stoppered vial)

When open aseptic processing is employed, there is a requirement to control the immediate and surrounding process environment (typically to ISO 5/Grade A).

Open Aseptic Processing Using RABS

Exposed product and containers should be protected under UAF, to maintain at least an ISO 5/Grade A environment with a background room classification of ISO 7/Grade B. Appropriate materials, equipment, and services should enter the ISO 5/Grade A and ISO 7/Grade B environments using appropriate decontamination steps. Personnel should be gowned appropriately.

Open Aseptic Processing Using Isolators

Isolators are decontaminated internally, typically using VHP or similar. No access is permitted other than via controlled alpha-beta docking ports and integrity-tested glove ports. The background room for a globally compliant facility should be ISO 8/Grade C. A Grade D environment classified as ISO 8 "in operation" as well as "at rest" is also possible.

定義與範例

開放製程的核心定義

當產品、物料或容器/封蓋表面暴露於即時製程環境，且此暴露可能影響產品品質或純度時，即為開放製程。開放製程需要更高的環境分級保護。

比喻：手術室與手術機器人

RABS 像是傳統手術室：外科醫師穿戴無菌衣進入，外部環境必須非常乾淨（ISO 7/Grade B）。隔離器像是手術機器人：醫師在外面遠端操控，外部環境要求可以降低（ISO 8/Grade C）。

2.8.2 Closed Processing / 封閉製程

Definition and Examples

Closed processing is a process condition when the product, materials, critical components, or container/closure surfaces are contained and separated from the immediate process environment within closed/sealed process equipment or enclosure.

Examples of closed processes include:

  • Closed sterile (post-sterilized-in-place) vessels
  • Closed material additions through canisters and alpha-beta ports
  • Closed sterilized (post-sterilized-in-place) pipework transporting product or materials
  • Closed single-use components/containers

When closed processing is employed, minimal controls are required for the immediate processing environment, provided that the integrity of the system is ensured through equipment design and operation and that there is appropriate monitoring to provide evidence for maintained integrity. A minimum of Grade D (qualified as ISO 8 "in operation" for US FDA) should be considered for such areas.

定義與範例

封閉製程的核心優勢

封閉製程的最大優點是大幅降低對環境的依賴：

  • 背景環境可降至 Grade D（最低要求）
  • 減少人員着裝要求
  • 降低 HVAC 系統建造和營運成本
  • 減少環境監測負擔

但前提是：系統完整性必須通過設計和監控來證明。

實務應用：開放 vs 封閉決策流程

在設計新製程時，報問自己：

  1. 產品在此步驟是否暴露於環境？
  2. 能否通過工程手段實現封閉？
  3. 封閉系統的完整性能否被監控與證明？

如果三個問題的答案都是「是」，封閉製程是較佳選擇；否則需要開放製程的高等級環境保護。

2.9

Integrated Facility Design

Zoning, material/personnel flow, segregation, lifecycle cost — p35–p36

Manufacturing Process Flow

The manufacturing process includes a sequence of manufacturing and work-in-progress storage steps en route to the creation of the finished product. This embraces unit process operations such as:

  • Weighing of components
  • Milling, mixing, formulation
  • Filtering
  • Transport of sterilized materials and components
  • Filling into containers
  • Transport of partially stoppered vials
  • Lyophilization
  • BFS (Blow-Fill-Seal)
  • Sterilizing, sealing, coding

The manufacturing process is normally supported by other functions close by: utilities, warehousing, inspection areas, offices, and laboratories.

Contamination Control Through Design

The design of each element of the manufacturing facility should contribute to minimizing product contamination risk. Contamination may be minimized by methods such as:

  • A clothing changing regime for personnel (separate gowning and de-gowning)
  • Pre-treatment of components and container/closures
  • Air filtration, airflow direction, and room pressurization
  • Personnel flow and material flow control

For personnel and materials to move from one area to another while maintaining protection for the product, engineers should consider the facility as a whole rather than as isolated parts.

Facility up-time should be optimized and it should be possible to perform maintenance and repair efficiently, especially if complex technology is employed—for example, by minimizing the need for interventions into the aseptic area.

The lifecycle cost of facilities, and not just the initial cost, should be considered. A higher initial cost using better materials may mean less operating and maintenance costs, resulting in a lower lifecycle cost.

製造製程流程與整合設計

整合設計的四大核心原則

  1. 人流與物流分離：人員和物料應有獨立的進入路徑，避免交叉污染。
  2. 潔淨度級聯：從低潔淨區到高潔淨區，逐步提升，每一層都有相應的控制措施。
  3. 設施可用性最佳化：維護區域應能夠在不影響無菌區域的情況下進入。
  4. 生命週期成本考量：不能只看初始建造成本，要考慮長期營運、維護、能源等總成本。

比喻：機場的動線設計

無菌製造設施的人流/物流設計就像機場：出境與入境分離、行李與乘客走不同通道、安檢區作為級聯關卡。同理，潔淨物料和髒污物料絕不應共用通道，人員進入無菌區前必須經過更衣階段（就像安檢）。

生命週期成本實例

一個使用較貴但耐久的316L不鏽鋼表面的設施，初始投資可能高出20-30%，但由於減少清潔、維修和停機時間，10年總成本可能反而更低。ISPE強調：不要只比較建造成本，要比較生命週期總成本。

思考練習：設施動線設計

如果您要設計一個新的無菌灌裝設施，請考慮以下動線：

  1. 原料從倉庫到配製區的路徑？
  2. 滅菌後的容器如何進入灌裝區？
  3. 人員從辦公區到 Grade B 的更衣階段？
  4. 維護人員如何不進入無菌區即可維修設備？
2.10

Other Considerations

Fire protection, emissions, noise, health & safety — p36–p37

Additional Facility Design Considerations

Additional considerations for facility design, which are outside the specific scope of this guide, include:

  • Means of escape — Emergency exit routes must be designed to allow rapid evacuation without compromising cleanroom integrity during normal operations.
  • Fire protection — Fire suppression systems must be compatible with cleanroom environments and pharmaceutical products.
  • Emissions — Air handling and exhaust systems must meet environmental regulations for particulate and chemical emissions.
  • Noise control — HVAC systems and production equipment should meet occupational noise exposure limits.
  • Health and safety — General occupational health and safety requirements must be integrated into the facility design.

其他設計考量

實務觀點：這些「非核心」要素往往是禁區痛點

這些項目雖然不在本指南的主要範圍內，但在實際工程設計中經常造成問題：

  • 消防：潔淨室內的灑水系統是污染源，需要特殊設計（如預作用式系統）。
  • 逃生通道：緊急出口不能使潔淨室壓差系統失效，但必須滿足建築法規。
  • 噪音：HVAC系統特別是高級別HEPA風機的噪音可能超過85dB。

比喻：買房時的「隱藏成本」

就像買房不能只看房價，還要考慮物業費、停車、社區安全等。無菌設施設計也一樣：消防、逃生、噪音控制這些「隱藏」需求如果在設計後期才發現，改造成本會非常高。

S

Section Summary / 章節總結

Key takeaways from Sections 2.6–2.10

Key Takeaways

  1. Harmonized Classification: Three parallel systems exist globally (EU Grade A-D, ISO 5/7/8, old US Class 100/10K/100K). Facilities serving multiple markets must design to the most conservative requirement across all applicable regulations.
  2. At Rest vs In Operation: EU Annex 1 defines limits for both conditions; US FDA is primarily "in operation." This distinction affects classification strategy, especially for Grade D areas.
  3. CNC Designation: "Controlled Not Classified" areas are increasingly common for support functions where formal classification is not required but access control and basic cleanliness are maintained.
  4. Operator Protection: Engineered controls (containment, isolators, automation) are preferred over PPE. The distinction between hazard and risk is fundamental to designing appropriate protection.
  5. Open vs Closed Processing: Open processes require ISO 5/Grade A at the point of exposure; closed processes can operate with Grade D background. The choice has significant cost and design implications.
  6. Isolator Advantage: Isolators allow background environment reduction from ISO 7/Grade B to ISO 8/Grade C while maintaining ISO 5/Grade A at the critical zone.
  7. Integrated Design: Personnel flow, material flow, zoning, and segregation must be designed holistically. The facility is a system, not a collection of isolated rooms.
  8. Lifecycle Cost: Higher initial investment in quality materials and design may yield lower total cost over the facility lifecycle through reduced maintenance, downtime, and energy consumption.

關鍵要點

  1. 調和分級：三大體系並行（EU Grade A-D、ISO 5/7/8、舊版 US Class）。面向多國市場時，必須採用最嚴格標準。
  2. 靜態與動態：EU 定義兩種條件，US以動態為主。Grade D 在歐美間的差異是設計陷阱。
  3. CNC 區域：控制但不分級，適用於檢驗、終端滅菌等支援區域。
  4. 人員防護：工程控制 > 管理控制 > PPE，這是防護層次的黃金原則。
  5. 開放與封閉：封閉製程可大幅降低背景環境要求，但必須證明系統完整性。
  6. 隔離器優勢：背景從 ISO 7 降至 ISO 8，關鍵區維持 ISO 5。
  7. 整合設計：人流、物流、分區、隔離必須整體考慮，設施是系統而非孤立房間。
  8. 生命週期成本：高品質初始投資可能帶來更低的總擁有成本。

自我檢核清單

  • 我能說出 Grade A/B/C/D 分別對應哪個 ISO 等級？
  • 我理解「靜態」與「動態」的差異及其對設計的影響嗎？
  • 我能解釋為什麼隔離器允許背景環境降級嗎？
  • 我能區分開放與封閉製程，並說出各自的環境要求嗎？
  • 我理解整合設計中人流/物流分離的重要性嗎？
2a

Chapter 2a: 3a. Process Equipment (3.1–3.2.3)

製程設備（上） | p37-p49

ISPE Baseline Guide Vol. 3 (3rd Ed.) | p37 – p49

學習目標 Learning Objectives

  1. 理解無菌製造製程設備的選型與整合原則，掌握性能、功能、結構、儀器、空氣品質、佈局及服務等七大考量面向
  2. 掌握典型無菌產品製程流程（從配製到檢查），區分無菌製程與最終滅菌製程之差異，並了解微生物負荷控制的關鍵風險因子
  3. 了解配製/秤量操作的集中式與分散式設計策略，以及交叉汙染防控措施與稱量方法選擇
  4. 理解滅菌後元件無菌控制的要求，包括傳遞方式、包覆策略及 ISO 5/Grade A 環境維護原則

Section Navigation

3.1 Introduction 3.2 Process Description 3.2.1 Dispensing & Weighing 3.2.2 Post-Sterilization Aseptic Control 3.2.3 Compounding Section Summary
3.1

Introduction

Process Equipment Considerations Overview | p37–p38

Original Text

3.1 Introduction

This chapter focuses on process equipment aspects. The use of integrated component washing, depyrogenation, siliconizing, and transport technology should be considered where applicable and feasible.

Process descriptions are provided to assist in understanding the process equipment considerations. Detailed User Requirements Specification (URS) documents should be the defining source for process equipment requirements and operating parameters. For catalog equipment, use of a data sheet in lieu of a URS may be acceptable.

The information contained within this chapter is intended to:

  • Recommend baseline practices intended to apply to sterile processes
  • Inform the facility design team of typical sterile product manufacturing schemes
  • Provide points for consideration in selecting sterile processing equipment
  • Provide points for consideration when integrating sterile processing equipment into the facility design

Section 3.2 provides a general description of each process stage and some aspects of process equipment selection for typical aseptic processing and processing with terminal sterilization. Illustrative process flows for both schemes, aseptic processing and terminally sterilized, are provided in Figure 3.1 and Figure 3.2, respectively.

Section 3.2 also includes information on equipment selection for isolators, and reference is made to RABS selection and to BFS operations. The use of separation and customization to supplement processes that allow direct personnel interventions should be utilized to the extent possible to minimize intervention impact.

General Points for Equipment Selection and Integration

  • Performance: This may include more detailed capacity attributes, but also covers specification of machine performance criteria, which controls product and container quality and cleanliness. Consideration should also be given to the extent of aseptic preparation activities that are routinely required for production use, due to the potential adverse impact of these manipulations on product sterility.
  • Functionality: This includes key functional attributes, such as the ability to maintain equipment from outside critical areas. Sampling and access points for qualification and validation testing should be incorporated in the equipment design.
  • Construction: This includes the durability, cleanability, and sterilizability of the materials of construction of the equipment that may contact product. Release of particulate from surfaces inside the cleanroom during operating and cleaning can be detrimental to the process; materials should be selected to minimize release.
  • Instrumentation: This includes a consideration of process parameter criticality and, therefore, the need for instrumented monitoring/detection. Instrumentation also may support a Process Analytical Technology (PAT) approach.
  • Air Quality: Equipment location within the facility is controlled by process and material flows, the criticality of operations performed, and by the consequent requirements for local and room air quality control. When designing an HVAC system, the heat loads and the particle generation from both operators and equipment should be considered along with humidity requirements.
  • Layout: Where possible, facility layouts should be designed to support functionality of the process equipment. Personnel and material flows needed for a particular process significantly affect the equipment layout and, therefore, the overall facility layout.
  • Services: Definition of both the instantaneous and daily demands of the equipment and on connecting services should be considered to support the sizing of the supporting services infrastructure. Consideration should be given to designs that allow maintenance access without impacting critical process areas.
導讀與實務解析

本節重點導讀

本章是 ISPE Vol.3 的製程設備核心章節，建立了設備選型的整體框架。重點不在於列舉特定品牌或型號，而是提供系統性的思考架構，讓設計團隊在選擇設備時有明確的評估面向。

核心概念：URS 是設備規格的根本依據

使用者需求規格書（User Requirements Specification, URS）是設備採購與設計的起點。URS 定義了「我們需要設備做什麼」，而非「設備能做什麼」。

對於目錄型設備（catalog equipment），可用設備規格表（data sheet）替代完整 URS，但仍需確認規格符合製程需求。

比喻：設備選型的七維雷達圖

想像設備選型如同為運動員做體能評估 — 不能只看單一指標。ISPE 提出的七個面向（性能、功能、結構、儀器、空氣品質、佈局、服務）就像雷達圖的七個軸，每個面向都需要達到最低基準才能確保整體適用性。

重點提示：設備選型七大面向摘要

  • 性能（Performance）：不只看產能，更要看機器對產品品質的控制能力，以及無菌準備操作的複雜度
  • 功能（Functionality）：維護能否從潔淨區外進行？取樣點和驗證接口是否已設計在內？
  • 結構（Construction）：產品接觸面（product contact surface）的材質必須耐久、可清洗、可滅菌、低粒子釋放
  • 儀器（Instrumentation）：關鍵製程參數需有監測能力，PAT 技術可即時監控品質
  • 空氣品質（Air Quality）：HVAC 設計須考慮設備和人員的熱負荷與微粒產生量
  • 佈局（Layout）：人流、物流決定設備佈局，佈局決定廠房佈局
  • 服務（Services）：公用系統的瞬時與日需求量須匹配，維護通道不應影響關鍵製程區

CDMO 應用觀點

對 CDMO 而言，設備選型的「功能」面向特別重要：

  • 多產品彈性：設備須能快速轉換不同容器型式（西林瓶、預充填針筒、卡匣）和不同產品
  • 轉換效率：changeover 時間直接影響產能利用率，CIP/SIP 能力是關鍵
  • 驗證負擔：每新增一個客戶產品就需要額外的設備驗證，選型時應考慮驗證的可擴展性
3.2

Process Description

Sterile Dosage Form Process Stages | p38–p42

Original Text

3.2 Process Description

The model process flow adopted as the basis of this chapter is that of a typical vial formulation, either aseptically processed or terminally sterilized. Designers may use this as the basis for design conditions for other processes and presentations—for example, APIs in bags or drums, glass or plastic ampoules, or syringes.

The general list of process stages for a sterile dosage form (not including equipment contact parts cleaning and preparation) is:

  • Dispensing
  • Post-sterilization aseptic control of components/change parts
  • Compounding (including aseptic compounding or buffer preparation, when applicable)
  • Sterile filtration
  • Sterile product bulk holding
  • Container preparation
  • Closure preparation
  • Transfer of components and equipment into aseptic area or across the isolator boundary
  • Filling and sealing
  • Transfer of uncrimped vials within aseptic area (for lyophilized product, transfer of partially stoppered vials from the filling line to lyophilizer, with subsequent transfer/unloading of fully stoppered, uncrimped vials)
  • BFS
  • Lyophilization, if applicable (this step is not assumed for terminally sterilized products)
  • Capping and crimping
  • Coding and code checking
  • Terminal sterilization
  • Inspection (may include cosmetic, particulate, container integrity, head space analysis, etc.)
  • Secondary packaging
  • Cleaning, sterilization and sanitization

Note: Application of continuous processing, automation and advanced processing techniques can eliminate or combine many of the above steps, to provide superior sterility assurance. For example:

  • For BFS, container/closure preparation and filling/stoppering are performed within the BFS filling machine.
  • For sterile APIs, it is usual for process steps—that is, from sterilize-in-place (SIP) of the process train through sterile bulk holding—to be truly closed, relying on the integrity of the closed system and of the associated cleaning and SIP techniques to ensure sterility.
  • Use of pre-sterilized, ready-to-use components can eliminate cleaning, sterilization, and aseptic staging steps for containers and closures.

Terminally Sterilized Products

Terminally sterilized products do not require the same level of environmental control as aseptically processed products. Despite these reduced requirements, steps should be taken to reduce the risk of introducing bioburden and/or endotoxin to the product. These steps commonly include sterilization and depyrogenation of components, sterilizing grade or bioburden reduction filtration of solution, and provision of LP/GAAS for filling operations. Bioburden control is particularly important when the terminal sterilization process has been validated for a specific bioburden, rather than using a standard overkill approach.

The background environment for filling should be ISO 8/Grade C, at a minimum.

Regulated companies may fill terminally sterilized products on the same production line as aseptically filled products, because of available production capacity. Aseptic environmental controls are then applied to maintain the more rigorous conditions required for aseptic filling of lyophilized product. However, this practice should not be construed as meaning that these controls are necessary for terminally sterilized products.

A documented risk assessment is recommended, to fully understand potential risks to a product.

Conditions that Elevate Bioburden Risk

  • Slow filling operations, including manual filling, where product and container/closure components are exposed to the environment for sustained durations
  • Open filling lines where operators are in close proximity to critical surfaces, product, and container/closure components
  • Use of semi-manual fill lines which require routine operator intervention
  • Long fill durations with products that are susceptible to bioburden; bulk bioburden reduction filtration may reduce bioburden levels and/or extend the allowable filling interval
  • Extended hold times prior to any pre-filtration or filling step

These risk factors can generally be mitigated through application of commonly available technology, such as automated filling systems with appropriate barrier technology.

導讀與實務解析

製程全貌：從秤量到包裝

本節描述的是一個典型西林瓶（vial）製程的完整流程。雖然以 vial 為模型，但設計者可以此為基礎延伸到預充填針筒、安瓶、軟袋等其他容器型式。

秤量/配料 → 配製/調配 → 除菌過濾 → 藥液暫存 → 充填/加塞 → 凍乾(如適用) → 封蓋/壓蓋 → 檢查 → 包裝

重點提示：微生物負荷（Bioburden）風險升高的五大情境

  1. 慢速充填/手動充填：產品暴露時間長，汙染風險倍增
  2. 開放式充填線：操作員靠近關鍵表面，人員是最大汙染源
  3. 半自動充填線：需要例行性人員介入操作
  4. 長時間充填：微生物敏感產品在長批次中風險累積
  5. 過濾前/充填前長時間暫存：微生物在暫存期間可能增殖

緩解措施：自動化充填系統 + 適當屏障技術（RABS/隔離器）是最有效的風險控制手段。

比喻：先進技術如何簡化流程

想像傳統製程像是在露天廚房做菜 — 每個步驟都暴露在環境中。而 BFS（吹灌封）技術像是在密封的自動販賣機裡完成容器成型、充填和密封，一氣呵成，大幅減少汙染風險。同樣地，使用預滅菌即用型（RTU）元件就像直接使用已消毒的免洗餐具，省去了自己清洗和消毒的步驟。

思考練習

  • 一家公司同時生產最終滅菌產品和無菌充填產品，為何可以共用同一條充填線？共用時應以哪個標準為設計基準？
  • 如果您的產品是奈米藥物（nano-medicine），為何 ISPE 建議可能需要重複進行微生物負荷降低過濾？
  • Figure 3.3 所示的凍乾產品製程流程中，哪些步驟是凍乾產品特有而液態產品不需要的？

CDMO 應用觀點

CDMO 的設備策略需要特別注意「共用線」的挑戰：

  • 產品排程邏輯：通常將最終滅菌產品排在無菌充填產品之後，因為清潔驗證需求不同
  • 環境控制切換：共用線意味著始終維持最高標準（ISO 5），這增加了營運成本但簡化了管理
  • 風險評估文件化：每位客戶的產品都需要獨立的風險評估文件，文件管理是一大挑戰
3.2.1

Dispensing and Weighing

Raw Material Handling Strategies | p42–p44

Original Text

3.2.1 Dispensing and Weighing

Components that undergo a subsequent sterilization step (e.g., filtration or terminal sterilization) are normally dispensed in an ISO 8/Grade C environment, at a minimum, with local protection (such as High Efficiency Particulate Air (HEPA) filtered unidirectional air) and the use of aseptic technique. The air cleanliness classification within the dispensary depends upon the process and product.

Consideration should be given to operator protection and mitigation of cross-contamination risk. In cases where additional separation/containment technologies (e.g., gloveboxes or isolators) are used for handling sensitive or high potency materials, lower background grade classifications may be appropriate.

Aseptically processed products that cannot be sterile filtered (e.g., sterile powders or suspensions) should be dispensed in an ISO 5/Grade A environment. In such cases, operator segregation via use of separation technology is generally considered to be necessary.

Two major concepts are generally applied in the industry for dispensing:

  • Centralized dispensing
  • Decentralized dispensing

Centralized dispensing is usually confined to solid actives and excipients. Decentralized dispensing is usually used for liquids (water, solvents, pH adjustment solutions), which are dispensed within the production areas (compounding room).

Advantages of Centralized Dispensing

  • It identifies dispensing as a separate process step that needs to be controlled.
  • It is easier to maintain a good working environment for operators.
  • Specialists with specific training and experience can be dedicated to one dispensing area, thereby reducing risk of mix-ups.

Advantages of Decentralized Dispensing

  • If compounding is for a single product, the risk of mix-ups and cross-contamination should be reduced, as only the specified raw materials are handled.
  • High hazard materials, that need to be contained (e.g., handled in gloveboxes) to protect operators, may be easier to control in a decentralized dispensing approach.

Liquid Measurement Methods

  • Gravimetric measurement may be performed using load cell(s), a balance, or a floor scale. The effect that attached components (cables, hoses, filter housing, valves) can have on the linearity and accuracy of the weighing range should be considered.
  • Volumetric measurement may be performed with flow meters or guided wave radar systems. If these types of instruments are used, calibration and desired accuracy should be reviewed.

Risk Reduction Methods for Cross-Contamination

  • Use of dedicated HVAC systems to handle airborne powders
  • Physical separation of dispensing areas
  • Cleaning (and inactivation, where appropriate) regime between products
  • System to separate dirty dispensing utilities from clean ones
  • System to compensate for room pressure changes due to loading of HVAC powder capture filters
  • Use of single-use disposable containers and weighing utensils
  • Use of appropriate local exhaust ventilation at point of generation sources

Enterprise Resource Planning (ERP) software may be used to control and track raw materials; these systems can be particularly advantageous for high volume operations that use many different types of raw materials.

導讀與實務解析

秤量/配料：製程的起點

秤量看似簡單，但它是製程中第一個可能引入交叉汙染的步驟。環境要求取決於後續是否有滅菌步驟可以「補救」。

重點提示：稱量方法的選擇陷阱

重量法（Gravimetric）注意事項：

  • 連接在容器上的管線、閥門、過濾器殼體會影響秤重的線性度和準確度
  • 夾套容器（jacketed vessel）的冷/熱介質充填狀態也會影響重量讀數

容積法（Volumetric）注意事項：

  • 導波雷達（guided wave radar）的準確度受容器設計和批次大小影響
  • 流量計需要定期校正，且流體特性會影響測量結果

比喻：集中式秤量像中央廚房

集中式秤量就像餐廳的中央廚房 — 由專業廚師統一備料，減少出錯。分散式秤量則像每桌自助取餐 — 適合單一菜色（單一產品），但多菜色時容易混亂。對於處理高危險性食材（高效價藥物），分散式反而更好，因為可以在專屬區域嚴格控管。

重點提示：交叉汙染防控的七道防線

  1. 專用 HVAC 系統處理粉塵
  2. 物理隔離秤量區域
  3. 產品間清潔（含去活化）程序
  4. 乾淨/髒汙器具分離系統
  5. 粉塵收集過濾器負載導致的壓差補償
  6. 一次性容器和秤量工具
  7. 產生源頭的局部排風

ERP 系統可實現即時庫存狀態、電子追溯矩陣和條碼追蹤，大幅降低秤量錯誤風險。

CDMO 應用觀點

  • 多產品設施的最大挑戰：不同客戶的 API 和賦形劑在同一秤量區交替操作，交叉汙染風險是稽核重點
  • 高效價藥物趨勢：越來越多客戶委託 ADC（抗體藥物複合體）等高效價產品，需要手套箱或隔離器，投資決策須提前規劃
  • 一次性系統（SUS）的策略：使用拋棄式秤量容器和工具可簡化清潔驗證，但增加耗材成本 — CDMO 需在每個客戶合約中權衡

核心概念：秤量環境等級的決定邏輯

關鍵原則：後續沒有「殺菌網」可接住的步驟，前端就必須做到最嚴格。

3.2.2

Post-Sterilization Aseptic Control of Components/Change Parts

Maintaining Sterility After Sterilization | p44–p45

Original Text

3.2.2 Post-Sterilization Aseptic Control of Components/Change Parts

For equipment that cannot be SIP, equipment and materials should be sterilized through pass-through style heat sterilizers, which open directly into an ISO 5/Grade A zone. Where sterilizers are not directly adjacent to the location where aseptic operations are performed, ISO 5/Grade A continuity should be maintained for the transfer of materials from the sterilizer to the place of storage or use.

Barrier protected carts which have active or passive airflow protection may be used; such carts should be qualified and routinely monitored. Where autoclave and oven carts are withdrawn from the sterilizer chamber into an ISO 7/Grade B room, there should be localized unidirectional ISO 5/Grade A airflow protection at the chamber outlet, so items may remain under these controlled conditions until the load has cooled. See Section 9.5.1 for equipment and component transfer on barrier and isolator style lines.

Autoclaved materials and components should be suitably wrapped to maintain sterile integrity of the contents from the point of removal from the autoclave to the point of use, including any intermediate staging steps. Multiple layer wrappings are recommended, as these provide redundant protection and permit removal of outer layers during transfer of materials into successively cleaner zones. The wrappings should permit air removal, steam ingress, and condensate removal as required for effective sterilization. Examples of suitable covering types include Tyvek, nonwoven Spunbond/Melt-blown/Spunbond (SMS) fabric sterilization wraps, sterilization bags, etc.

Items that are pre-sterilized by other methods, such as gamma irradiation or ethylene oxide, should be protected with appropriate wrappings to maintain their sterile integrity from the completion of the sterilization process until transfer into the ISO 5/Grade A environment. These items should be passed into the aseptic area via dedicated interlocked transfer hatches designed to prevent bio-contamination of the ISO 5/Grade A environment.

The packaging should be subjected to thorough surface disinfection—for example, using liquid chemical, VHP, or electron beam (e-beam)—which is validated for the control of bio-contamination of the ISO 5/Grade A environment. The transfer of the wrapped items into the ISO 5/Grade A zone should be performed in such a way as to ensure that the outer wrap can be taken off without introducing bio-contamination into the ISO 5/Grade A zone where product, product contact surfaces, containers or closures are exposed.

導讀與實務解析

滅菌後的無菌維護：最容易被忽略的風險環節

元件滅菌「成功」只是起點 — 從高壓鍋取出到實際使用之間的轉運過程，才是無菌保證的真正考驗。

核心概念：滅菌後物料轉運的三大原則

  1. 連續 ISO 5 保護：從滅菌器到使用點，物料始終處於 ISO 5/Grade A 氣流保護下
  2. 多層包覆策略：多層包裝提供冗餘保護，每進入更潔淨的區域就脫去一層外包裝
  3. 互鎖傳遞設計：預滅菌物品透過互鎖傳遞艙進入無菌區，防止環境交叉汙染

比喻：洋蔥式穿衣法

多層包覆策略就像登山的洋蔥式穿衣法 — 每一層都有特定功能。最外層是防汙層（在非潔淨區穿著），中間層是保護層，最內層是無菌層（在 ISO 5 區域最後才拆開）。每進入一個更乾淨的區域，就像從戶外進入室內，脫掉一件外套。

核心概念：包覆材料的雙重需求

滅菌包覆材料必須同時滿足兩個看似矛盾的需求：

  • 滅菌穿透性：允許空氣排出、蒸汽滲入、冷凝水排除（否則滅菌不完全）
  • 微生物屏障性：滅菌完成後必須阻擋微生物進入（否則無菌性被破壞）

常見材料：Tyvek（杜邦特衛強）、SMS 不織布滅菌包、滅菌袋等。這些材料的微孔結構允許蒸汽通過但阻擋微生物。

思考練習

  • 為什麼高壓鍋推車從滅菌器取出進入 ISO 7/Grade B 房間時，必須在出口處提供局部 ISO 5 氣流保護？
  • 如果您使用預滅菌的即用型（RTU）注射器元件，表面消毒驗證的關鍵挑戰是什麼？
  • 「屏障保護推車（barrier protected cart）」如何同時實現物料保護和操作便利性？

CDMO 應用觀點

  • RTU 元件的戰略價值：對 CDMO 而言，使用預滅菌即用型容器和膠塞可大幅減少洗滌/滅菌設備投資和驗證負擔，同時縮短產品轉換時間
  • 滅菌後暫存管理：多客戶產品排程下，滅菌後物料的暫存時間管理是挑戰 — 需要明確的最長暫存時間限制和追蹤系統
  • 穿越式滅菌器佈局：CDMO 廠房設計時，穿越式高壓鍋/烘箱的位置直接影響多條充填線的操作效率
3.2.3

Compounding

Formulation and Mixing Operations | p45–p49

Original Text

3.2.3 Compounding

The purpose of compounding is to formulate together API, excipients, and solvent components, to be subsequently filled. This may involve simple liquid mixing or dissolution of a solid active. It also may include more complex operations such as emulsification or liposome formation. Water for Injection (WFI) should be used as the solvent for most aqueous-based sterile products. Low endotoxin purified water is sometimes used for sterile ophthalmic and nasal products.

Product contacting surfaces of equipment and components (such as vessels, housings, and process piping) should be cleaned prior to use. See Section 3.2.15 for additional details on cleaning and sterilization.

If the subsequent compounding is an aseptic process, process equipment should be sterilized using a validated sterilizing cycle. The integrity of the sterile boundary should be ensured from the completion of sterilization through the end of processing.

Air cleanliness and cross-contamination prevention should be considered. Use of localized HEPA (ISO 5/Grade A air supply) protection is recommended to protect non-sterile product contact surfaces areas (e.g., vessel openings), where possible. For example, in many cases HEPA filters required to meet area cleanliness classifications can be located over tank manways, to reduce risk of contamination of product contact surfaces.

When handling dry powders, the design should minimize release of any fine particles into the air. Use of containment devices may be appropriate.

If, for product reasons, an aseptically processed product cannot be sterile filtered or sterilized by some other means (e.g., bulk heat) after compounding, then the charging of raw materials should be performed in an ISO 5/Grade A environment, preferably using a RABS or closed isolator. Special consideration should be given to the airflow inside the barrier when handling fine powders, as air speeds lower than 0.45 meters/second might be beneficial to better control the process.

Compounding Sequence
